Raj Dixit< /user_name>
<date>1499047051217<//date><Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Saw the Folsom Pro Rodeo for the first time. A very enjoyable show, fun for the whole family, capped off with a fun fireworks display. Yes, it's hot, but what else is new in Folsom in July? It's crowded, but the more the merrier. Only downside is that it takes a while to leave due to the jammed paid parking lot. Still, a great experience. Recommended.</Review>

<rating>5</rating>< review>
Know what a nightmare it is to find a place where you feel good about keeping your things for a little while or longer? It's so nice that you can go to A-1 and feel entirely safe and happy about where you're storing your material goods.

Hemingway was talking about his favorite bodega in "A Clean and Well Lighted Place" but that idea fits here too. Right by the freeway, super safe, super clean. It's just a bonus that the manager is ex law enforcement.

A few cool things I haven't run into before:

1) Everything is inside! If you've ever used an outside storage area, dirt and pests somehow seem to find their way in... Also better temperature control inside.

2) Elevators that open all the way to the outside, super easy for loading/unloading.

3) I went over 10 times in a month, I never got a cart with a crazy wheel :)

4) Music playing inside the building, very cheery.

10 Stars! Entirely exceeded my expectations.

Thanks for having me!</review>

< Rating>

<Review>A wonderful intermodal station, although it is a bit labyrinthine.  The main waiting room is a beautiful throwback with Morris chairs and echo-y big brown floor tiles.  The one trouble spot is the tunnel up from which connects to the elevated tracks...but if you keep walking, you access the red line and up and out to the bus loading area (Patsaouris Plaza) that is open to the air.  Btw, stop in to One Gateway building lobby...it‚Äôs beautiful.

< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>
<text>Union Station is a central transportation hub to a variety of locations. You will find Los Angeles Metro stations here (Blue Red Purple and Gold Line), Express and local bus service, Flyaway service to local airports and Amtrak.

Whether you are traveling via any of those modes of transportation or not, this is a location to visit to admire the history and architecture. Marble floors, hanging lighting, high ceilings, mosaic tiling on the patio outside near Trax restaurant. There is a piano at the end of the sitting area before the small food court, inviting anyone to sit and tickle the ivories. You never know what you will hear: classical, jazz, show tunes...even boogie boogie and classic rock tunes that feature piano.

Additionally, the Grand Ballroom is located at the street entrance, as well as Trax Restaurant, several food establishments, and a newspaper stand. There is a convenience/grocery store near the entrance to the trains that sells a variety of items and food. Definitely worth the time to visit...< /text>< Response>
None</Response>

Let's see... where do I begin....
The LA Metro Transit system is THE ABSOLUTE WORST. Goldline, Red line, Explo Line, Blue Line -- All the lines.

Unlike the rest of their world, their constantly broken down trains and rail lines arrive every 20 minutes or so morning, day and night -- unlike their advertised 5 minute transit arrival times.
On top of arriving late every day, they shorten the train by 2 cars so you are ABSOLUTELY JAMMED & CRAMMED ON THE TRAIN with other people.
The drivers love to slam on the breaks.
People are smoking blunts on the goldline and redline like it's a full time job. The police do absolutely nothing about it. Even amidst the complaints. But why would they? Theyre paid a time and half to sustain the most mundane job on the planet. They just don't care..

<rate>5</rate><Review>TL;DR: I use the Midway location.  Have visited ~10 times.  I like it.  The staff is friendly.

So I use this place (Midway/Sports Arena location) for Cryo when I'm in San Diego.  It has friendly staff and a chill (pun fully intended) laid back, California vibe.  It is geared more toward athletes and ex-military (they offer a military discount) members (although all welcome, ofc) than the usual, spa-type cryo place.  So it's not "nightclub as health club-type place" it's more "old school"/fewer frills and therefore with better pricing.

The staff will show you how to use the equipment and get you set up.  They explain everything you need to know and if you need to go over it again, they do.

Since I started Cryo, I have noticed improved health and mood and I generally "feel better" on a day to day basis.  I do daily sessions here (and back home) for 5 minute sessions.

There are speakers in the chamber and you can plug in your Apple/Android phone and listen to music during your session.  I pick a song that is 5 or so minutes long to keep my mind occupied.

One thing I note is that about 15 minutes after a session is over, I am suddenly hungry, which likely has to do with the calorie burn.<//Review><pics>None</pics>< Response>
None< /Response>

I love this spot! The owner is chill as f---- trying to get the latest and greatest for recovery, and boy does it work.

I've had many hip issues and they give you a portable fan to take in while you, "chill". That fan helps target problem areas and makes it colder cuz of the wind chill factor. My problem areas haven't been able to get the attention they need because they're in awkward spots, so targeting them with that fan gave me some relief I haven't been able to really experience with other practices (PT, massage, acupuncture, chiropractor, and other cryo places that aren't full body). When I got out I couldn't stop laughing. I got some kind of rush and just kept laughing for 30 seconds. It was great. Lol

Tried the LED Red Light Therapy Bed too. I've used the portable ones before that work too, but this bed is awesome. I do Muay Thai and I really feel this and cryo help me recover faster

When you put your body through hell you need this to keep it at its peak performance.      Happy to be going here to keep myself tip top< /Review>

< Review>
This a review of only their coffee after 3 separate visits. The only roast they had on drip was a dark roast, which is strange for a 3rd wave coffee shop. A medium dark, at least, should be the standard. 2 out of the 3 times, the espresso was over-extracted and had burnt-popcorn taste that was so strong the milk (which had a nice microfoam) barely masked it. I didn't ask about the espresso roast, so I couldn't say when it was roasted or how dark it was, but it honestly might just be a re-calibration issue. I don't get the feeling that they are consistently checking the shots to check the extraction time and ratios.

Anyway, the lattes are not worth the 4.50, they charge for them.< /Review>

< Text>
I ate here yesterday for the first time. Some colleagues and I were looking for somewhere new to eat and Jeff's seemed rather "inviting" with the favorable reviews.  After the visit here are my takes:

Exterior - The restaurant is in a strip mall with various other stores and restaurants.  Seeing the outside I really was not sure what to expect since it looked a little drab.

Interior - The place is kind of small; however, the restaurant is nicely decorated inside.  It definitely made an inviting atmosphere and Jeff meeting us at the door and seating us was a great first impression.

Service - Our waitress was very nice and efficient.  The team also worked together extremely well and added to the wonderful atmosphere.

Food - OK now the reason you go to a restaurant is definitely the food, and the food at Jeff's was top notch.  The only complaint I have is that we waited quite a bit for the food; however, it was certainly worth the wait.  The risotto was perfectly cooked and was full of flavor.  I had the sea scallops with asparagus and saut√©ed mushrooms.  My entr√©e was also perfectly cook, and if I had to pick one negative it was that it could have been seasoned just a little more.  One of the other members of my table had the brussel sprouts as their side and shared with me and they were incredible as well.

All in all I will definitely be back as often as I can afford it, because the misses were small and their wins were excellent!</Text>

< text>
This is the 3rd location I've been to, and it is up to par. Staff had good customer service, food took a little longer than were used to (esp for the place only having 3 groups already eating inside). But, everything was as good as we remembered. Substitutions were accurate as requested.Very happy to report that both restrooms(single occupancy) have baby changing stations (with bag hooks on the corners), and coat/purse hooks on the back of the door. The restroom on the right has a urinal inside. Both were clean. You have choice of booths, tables with loose chairs, a bar height table with chairs, and a combo of both. We were able to hold our 6 month old in the booth without too much fumbling.  Outdoor seating is nicer than most, has patio heaters mounted above which were more than adequate (and it was drizzling today), low 50's.< /text>

We love The Habit in Murrieta, Ca! Reasonably priced and good food! Variety of drinks including soda, tea, and lemonade.

I love the Monterey Sandwich which is a double patty and cheese on toasted sourdough bread. Delicious!

Clean tables and restrooms. Outdoor seating available. They give you a blinking buzzer when your food is ready, great for a fast food restaurant.

Customer service is excellent! My son realized that his Monterey sandwich only had one Patty. They allowed him to eat it and gave him a brand new sandwich for free.

The Habit is the best!<//review>

< user_id>
107136176059594037309< /user_id>
<text>Let's begin by saying that The Habit is not going to be habit forming, for what we had, was only one more on a long chain of similar items. Not a revolutionary eatery by a long shot. Yes, the investment is there, plenty of bells and whistles, and the prices way up there to reassure the patron that this is indeed the place to be. Food selected for a first time visit:
2 Albacore Sandwhiches with Teriyaki sauce on the side (requested to avoid over sweetening things), $6.99: a fish sandwich with a desire to come across with a higher pedigree. Edible, a little tiny bit dried, and very slippery, like if it wanted to head on back to the sea in which it was found, or was it farmed? Who knows these days? The wheat bun was small, nothing to clap about it, did I hear anyone say: chippie? The sourdough bread, which was for the second sandwich a little nicer, but no different than any sourdough available at the regular markets. 3 Stars.
2 Double Chars, $4.85 each: for the sake of expediency must be, they are called double char, and this is no more, no less, what one would get at any place they decide to stop to get a burger, nothing really special about the beef used, and much less the ingredients that accompanied this item. 3 Stars.
2 French Fries, $4 both: Yes, they were crispy, but once again, who doesn't make them crispy when they first get out of the fryer. Been there, tasted that, no first price for the best fries here. 3 Stars.
2 Sodas, $1.90: all you can drink of carbonated offerings, this one favoring Pepsi, Coke? I forgot. Carbonation was not too shabby. 3.5 Stars.
People that worked in the place, were very nice and one specially nice lady, saw us outside at a table and went inside and got us ketchup for the fries, we got a little humbled there, for we felt she went out of her way to be nice. We felt mighty good about her help.
The Habit is out there, lines on this weekday a little busy, but then they slowed down, for we had arrived at the end of the lunch rush? Will we be coming back to The Habit? And what about the name, is it for people to get used and repeat their business? Who knows how they established the name, but habit forming it is not. Total: $34 with tax.
3 Stars.< /text><resp>None< /resp>< gmap_id>
